I thought start up ment not working at all wonâ€™t turn on
Startups and new businesses now have completely forgotten the principal of the MVP (minimum viable product). Instead of trying to match all the features of all competitors, build all the greatest bells and whistles, and have a totally complete product with every dream feature from launch you need to specialize and do the basics right first. If you're starting an EV company that means find a market segment with a gap (small sporty cheap EVs, Light Truck EVs, School Bus/School Van EVs, Fire Engine/Ladder Vehicle EVs, Ambulance EVs, &c). Figure out what the core essentials of that one thing are and focus all your energy on nailing those things perfectly. Then launch that simple, lower spec but really great product for the use case and capture a core market. Then with that add in a new feature set, capability, product range, or other addition in cycles every year/two years until you get where you plan to go. Since you're now working from a solid platform all the future work will actually be really good because you're not trying to fix a million little bugs, bad features, and PR issues while trying to make V2 of the product. It's not flashy, exciting, or ego boosting, but you actually get fans & a good reputation to trade on and that's invaluable for a startup.

I only know that there are newer firmware versions when I had a chit-chat with a Xanh SM's driver (a taxi provider of Vingroup). I asked "why? why couldnt I see any notification from Customer Service?", the driver just told me to go to forum (host by Vinfast) to update information. I also received the same answer from a Vinfast CS Staff. I sill dont know why they do not notify us about firmware update. No SMS, No Emal, No Call, No App Notification. Nothing   Second issue for me, it happend at the beginning of Ferb - 2024, a few day before our Tet vacation, so I wanted to make up my car a little bit. She needed an firmware update, and when everything's done, I found out that the e-Sim was not working. The car considered me as a guest, and I could not log in my account. So I brought her back to Service Center. After hours of waiting, they said they run a diagnostic, but could not detect the problem. It's last day of old Lunar Year, so they said there would be a new version of firmware after Tet vacation and I should come back at that time. OK!!!!!!   I waited a few day after Tet Vacation (because I received no notification about firmware update). Here is the 3rd fuckin' problem with Vinfast Customer Service. I came to Service Center at 11 AM. The Staff asked me "Do you have a appointment?", I said "No", so he gave me a number and told me to wait. 15 minutes - Nothing happend 30 minutes - I saw they called nobody name  50 minutes -  sit & wait  55 minutes - a car owner asked CS Staffs when they can start handover process (because we were waiting for a hour, and it's lunch time), but the staff just look at his computer, say something like "wait, just wait", then disappeared, all of them, the CS, the engineer, the worker. I had been there for 55 minutes but with most of car owner in that room, it's up to hours. Some of them are taxi driver of Xanh SM, that means they earned no single penny in that morning, did not even have a lunch (because they could not hand-over their car to Service Center, so they had to sit there and wait, could not go to anywhere). Meanwhile, VINFAST CUSTOMER SERVICE Staff, they had a good lunch, took a good nap, then came back to work after 1 PM with a good smell coffee. After ~ 120 minutes of waiting - it's my turn, FINALLY! Another process as same as my last vist. When it's done CS Staff told me that the new firmware "works well", my problem with e-Sim will be supported online. Here in Canada, we got Hyundai cars before the United States. We had the Hyundai Pony and the Hyundai Stellar. 1984-1986 cars with manual chokes, no catalytic converters, and if you can get your head around this, they had POINTS IGNITION! I had to change points and condenser and set dwell on my 1985 car!  About a week after buying the Stellar (a 9-year-old car) for $100, it was a rainy cold night. Rear window defroster, front defrost fan, wipers, headlights, ignition circuit loads. Bosch alternator under the hood. Voltage gauge was dropping..... I thought it was an instrumentation fault until the lights got dim and the engine cut out. Fortunately, I was on a hill and was able to turn off all the electrical loads and get the car rolling and re-start it by dropping the clutch.  Bosch alternator - nothing wrong with it - but only rated for 40A. Rear defroster, 20A. Front blower fan, 20A. Wipers, 10A. Headlights and parking lamps, say 15A. Ignition, say 5A. Whatever the case, the alternator, from the factory, was not big enough to run the car on a cold rainy night. What a joke.  I had a 105A alternator from an old Volare police car. It was almost a direct bolt-in. Started up my Hyundai Stellar with the cop car alternator installed and the voltage gauge was solidly pegged around 14V no matter what I turned on in the car. And this was a "luxury" car with air conditioning (never worked) and power everything. 40 amp Bosch alternator from the factory. Jesus wept.

Here's the truth! Vinfast is not new having manufactured electric vehicles (EVs) since 2018 when the first fully electric motorbike Klara was made. So far, VinFast has made tens of thousands of EVs including VinFast e34 (a smaller version of VF8), VF5, VF8, VF9, and especially VinBus known as VinFast fully electric public buses carrying 50-60 passengers at a time. Most importantly, a fleet of over 120 units of VinBus since December 2021, has been providing service between the cities, every day from morning to night - from 5:00 to 21:00, 7 days a week transporting a total of over 150 million passengers in Vietnam (equivalent to about half of the total US population) - average 300,000 passengers per day. Surprisingly, NOT a single unit of VinBus catching fire or exploding or losing control, has been reported so far! Also, tens of thousands of units of VinFast e34 and VF8 have been on the road safely in Vietnam since 3/2021 and 9/2022, respectively. Similarly, NOT a single unit of the Vinfast EVs catching fire or exploding or losing control, has been reported! This clearly solidified the quality and safety standards of Vinfast EVs. Have any other EV makers achieved what Vinfast did? Go figure! Technically, YouTuber Sandy Munro in one of his VF8 videos, did talk about Vinfast's patented technology for its EV battery isolation. According to CTIF (International Association of Fire and Rescue Services), up to 40,000 gallons of water is needed to put out a fire in an electric car like Tesla! Don't take my word for it. Look it up for yourself. EVs are supposed to be environmentally friendly, but what's the point of using 40,000 gallons of water to put out only one EV like Tesla? What do you think?

I really liked this review. The only part I dislike about electric car reviews that happened in this video specifically is when a manufacturer says they'll fix things with a software update. Comparing this car to early video game releases seems problematic in that vein. A video game has zero chances of harming me or people around me, a video game is also entirely made of software. This car is not made entirely of software, it's made of many hundreds if not thousands of individual components and no manufacturer should ever get to slide on faults with "we'll fix it with a software update". Much like the Chevy Bolt battery, they attempted to fix it with "software" and failed because the failure was entirely physical, waiting for the real fix to come (in the form of a recall of the part) people lost cars and had homes catch on fire. The lack of acceleration, the faulty driver assist, could all be down to using faulty or inferior hardware but are brushed away as software by the manufacturer. Even the lack of a stop/start button might seem trivial but it seems like a cost cutting measure more than a convenience thing. It's also not intuitive as you've shown in the video, in a world where people confuse the gas peddal and brake peddal and harm people because of that, having a clear and visible start/stop button is just sensible.

I have the feeling that they are having what a lot of Asian car companies that try to do a very complex programming task using people that do not use the product. I have had companies in Asia totally screw up the software as they hire people with very high degrees but do not own the product. In this case own a car.   I had a case of car speakers made in Korea and the customers were blowing them up and in North America. I was the person in charge of the warranty department and QC.  The company said they had brilliant people designing the product. They tested with very loud music. Cannone in the 1812 Overture.   This was in the mid 1980s.. They sent an engineer to out office in Vancouver. That day we were replacing the speakers in a young lady's Mustang. We were taking out hers and putting in some JBLs.  I took the Asian engineer to the car. and asked him to play his cassette and show me the volume. I listened for a few seconds znd stopped his demo. I fund the young lady's Led Zeppelin 2 tape and slammed that it in cranked the system into clipping.  To 11 so to say.  He leaped out of car shouting "You people crazy".. But the next batch of speakers did not blow up within an hour of new.  Apparently, on the way to the airport he bought several copies of Led Zeppelin 2.   My point of telling you this is that this story car shows all the symptoms of having the lead software designer not being a car owner themselves. That the while the speaker company tested with classical music instead of heavy metal it appears they were doing the engineering Asian style. Where the lead guy almost never touches the product. .That they do everything from theory. And they did it in a big rush. Using a team of people who also do not own cars doing their testing and reporting to someone only driving a desk.  Now they have to go through decades of product improvement very fast. Most of these look to me to be software issues and a poor choice of spring rates and shocks. I am not saying they are stupid. But I often see the attitude with the bosses there that they believe their testers are just being too picky.  Now that the reviewers here are figuratively handing them their asses, they will fix these issues.  But because of this, there will be some really bad reviews on their cars that will not go away. This will badly impact their sales in North America.   Toyota seemed to go through the same thing with the Toyopet in the 1950s where they did not test it properly and had to pull out of the US market for like a decade.  My feeling is that the will essentially catch up with these issues as they are not insurmountable. But they have to undercit the Tesla 3 on price to have any hope of good sales.

The chimes and the driving aids trickled down from the trucking industry that had it first. Too many people suing companies over truck crashes because they decided to run out in front of an 18wheeler expecting it to stop the same. Most drivers find all these systems a major defect and distraction. Could you imagine listening to those things all day every day while you work and try to focus?? In turn this has ran off a lot of the veteran drivers, and replaced with new drivers that rely on those systems rather than having the experience and skill level to maneuver professionally. Also causing roads to be more unsafe. This also can be contributed to higher demand for drivers, higher rates for freight, higher costs for operations of companies that have to buy these systems by law, which means higher prices in stores. Thanks to all the Karen's, you can now see this in consumer cars with higher prices due to all the safety systems on them. What goes around comes around.

The start-up sequence isn't that bad as you perform those steps subconsciously before turning the key. The only thing missing here is the key.  When I get into my car, first I close the door, then I put my seatbelt on (as my hand is still near that area anyway), put my foot on the brake while putting the key in the ignition (and my other foot is on the clutch as I have a stickshifter), and then turn the key to start.  Now I can imagine that people can get into issues when they first want to start the car and then put the seatbelt on afterwards. I guess a lot of people switch those two steps around; which would cause this particular car to not start. In this respect I can't fault that Vietnamese company for putting safety first in making sure that the occupants have their seatbelts on before the car will start. ğŸ™‚  Back to the show... If the passengers feel nauseous/uncomfortable, that means terrible engineering on Vinfast's side. The suspension system of a passenger car is usually tuned for comfort. Feeling seasick in a car for example means that vibrations around 0.2 Hz are not well dampened, which was a problem solved decades ago. Other vibration frequencies can also annoy your eyes, nose or heart. There is a set of frequencies that the car's suspension system should handle very well, and therefore the car should be tested against. I don't think such a small company owns all the needed test benches for that. But they can at least get their prototypes tested at big manufacturers' facilities or universities for the final tuning of the suspension system.

@donut, regard to your complain about accelerator pedal. Vinfast car has a very interesting feature. If you jump or sudendly push on its accelerator pedal, the car will stop or reduce speed, instead of accelerate. The reason is that Vinfast car identifies you press the wrong pedal: you want to push the brake pedal but you push the accelerator pedal. It is one of safety feature of Vinfast cars.

Like its parent company, VinFast has grown at an eye-searing rate. VinGroup was founded in 1993, and VinFast itself was only started in 2017. We are very proud that our country can build a car on its own. But, VIN slave made us change that mind. Whenever a car has a problem, we usually pay attention to when they fix the problem, or when someone posts a question like should I buy a vinfast car. We often take risks like it is full of bugs, it takes time to stabilize. (Because a car in Vietnam is a pretty big asset, not just a means of transportation, you can look up the GDP of my country.). The first question he asked is how to start this car! He then said, "We have been making cars for over 100 years!" This just showed how clueless he is. Yes, we Americans have been making cars for over 100 years, but they are ICE cars, NOT electric ones! Electric vehicles are totally different from ICE vehicles. The drivetrain of an ICE vehicle contains up 2,500 moving parts, while the drivetrain of an electric vehicle contains only 20 moving parts. Electric motors are typically powered by two moving parts and are driven by single-speed â€œtransmissionsâ€ without gears. This is why many traditional ICE car manufacturers including Toyota are facing many tough challenges including new technology when transitioning from making ICE vehicles to electric ones. Obviously, Vinfast is not perfect, neither is Tesla, and Tesla has been making EV for over 15 years!
Vinfast is not a good EV? Think again. Tesla as the leading EV maker in the world has been making EVs for over 15 years, but Tesla cars are not immune from serious problems. According to Forbes, over 4 million (81% of 5,093,690) Tesla cars had been recalled since January 2022, which meant 4 out of 5 cars Tesla made, had certain problems from breaking and seat belt flaws to battery and software issues. Also, the Washington Post on 06/12/2023 reported, there have been 736 Tesla crashes as a result of Tesla Autopilot since 2019 when it first started - average 147 tesla crashes per year or 3 Tesla crashes per week! It's shocking, isn't it? That's not it; over 3 weeks ago on 6/11/2023, a footage of Tesla "phantom break" causing 8-car crash pileup emerged. Tesla Autopilot Full Self-Driving (FSD) caused a Tesla to suddenly stop for no apparent reason, in the middle of a lane under the San Francisco Bay Bridge. Sadly, Tesla has publicly put the blame on the driver for using Tesla "Full Self-Driving" (FSD) mode because it's NOT actually full self-driving despite its name. Duh! According to Kron4 report on 6/14/2023, a white Tesla was fully engulfed in flames after a single-vehicle collision. The vehicle appeared completely destroyed after the flames were extinguished. A 44-year-old mother and her 13-year-old daughter were killed in a fiery crash when their white Tesla hit a tree. The husband, who was not in the car said, "Whatever comes out of all this about how they ended up where they did, it shouldnâ€™t have exploded, caught fire whatever you want call it, so quickly that they couldnâ€™t get out." Women in general tend to drive more carefully, especially when driving with their children in their vehicles, which explained why women often pay less for car insurance than men. The cause of this Tesla crash killing the 44-year-old mother and her 13-year-old daughter, remains a mystery. Tesla cars are not perfect despite the fact that Tesla has been making EVs for over 15 years! No EVs are perfect, but the ones with fewer serious problems are better. It's your choice. Yes, we Americans have been making cars for over 100 years, but they are ICE cars, NOT electric ones! Electric vehicles are totally different from ICE vehicles. The drivetrain of an ICE vehicle contains up 2,500 moving parts, while the drivetrain of an electric vehicle contains only 20 moving parts. Electric motors are typically powered by two moving parts and are driven by single-speed â€œtransmissionsâ€ without gears. This is why many traditional ICE car manufacturers including Toyota are facing many tough challenges including new technology when transitioning from making ICE vehicles to electric ones. Obviously, Vinfast is not perfect, neither is Tesla, and Tesla has been making EV for over 15 years!

I'm not saying that this car is a result of over-regulation, but some of the features would definitely represent a politician's sense of a "good idea so let's do it", and the possible results that may not be unintended. Actually, that the car tries to get you back in your lane if you're not using blinker, is quite common on at least euro spec cars. It's a basic functionality at the very bottom (level 1) of self driving.  As far as I can remember, at least the 3 last cars I've leased had this functionality. It might not be to your liking, and it might not even be common in US spec cars for all I know, but it's a common feature in modern cars.

History has countlessly demonstrated the path for foreign or unproven companies to experience product growth.    Introduce a cheap, reliable, product that appeals to the masses because they're more likely to consider price over style/design/brand. For example in the US look at the ford model t in 1920s, Honda in the 1960s, Toyota and nissan in the 70s, hyundai and kia in the 90s-2000s. They started with cheap, decent cars bought by people unconcerned with brand image. As they improved design, reliability, and image theyve become some of the most popular vehicles on the road.   Did they not ask themselves " will people buy an inferior $50k car from an unknown manufacturer when market competitors offer more at the same price?"

the throttle complaint reminded me of a new machine I worked with that had an electronic throttle.  there were operators who would stand there twisting on the throttle control and adjusting the desired output numbers, and complaining that the machine wasn't responding.  the machine was programmed to wait one full second before implementing any throttle changes, to let the operator to get the correct output set before adjusting the throttle.   I can see the benefit of a slight throttle lag, to even out any bounce from being oversprung and under damped.  I've seen people driving cabover trucks get into an oscillation pattern as their foot bounces on the throttle. so having it average out the throttle input over half a second would reduce that bounce.
